Square one,"<b>Meaning:</b> The very beginning; the starting point. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likely from board games or early radio football broadcasts where the field was divided into squares. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The deal fell through, so we are back to square one."
Stone's throw,<b>Meaning:</b> A very short distance. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> The distance a person can physically throw a stone. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The hotel is just a stone's throw from the beach.
Stretch the truth,"<b>Meaning:</b> To exaggerate or lie slightly. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for pulling the truth until it becomes distorted. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He said he caught a giant fish, but I think he was stretching the truth."
Strike a chord,<b>Meaning:</b> To cause someone to feel sympathy or enthusiasm; to remind someone of something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From music; playing a note that resonates with another. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Her story about growing up in a small town really struck a chord with the audience.
Sweep it under the rug,<b>Meaning:</b> To hide a problem or an embarrassing fact instead of dealing with it. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal image of a lazy cleaner hiding dirt under a carpet. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> You can't just sweep these complaints under the rug and hope they go away.
Swing for the fences,<b>Meaning:</b> To take a big risk in order to achieve a huge success. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From baseball; trying to hit a home run over the outfield fence. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> We're swinging for the fences with this new product launch.
Take the plunge,<b>Meaning:</b> To decide to do something difficult or important after thinking about it for a long time. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for jumping into deep water. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> They finally decided to take the plunge and get married.
That ship has sailed,"<b>Meaning:</b> It is too late to take an opportunity. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for missing a boat that has already left the port. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I wanted to buy that house, but someone else already did. That ship has sailed."
The grass is always greener on the other side,"<b>Meaning:</b> Other people's situations always seem better than your own. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A proverb dating back to ancient times about envy. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He quit his job for a new one, but now he misses his old coworkers; the grass is always greener."
The jury is still out,<b>Meaning:</b> A decision has not yet been reached; the result is still unknown. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the legal system; when the jury leaves the courtroom to deliberate. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The jury is still out on whether the new law will actually help the economy.
The world is your oyster,<b>Meaning:</b> You have the ability and opportunity to do anything you want. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From Shakespeare's 'The Merry Wives of Windsor'; implies you can find the 'pearl' inside the world. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> You’ve just graduated with top honors; the world is your oyster.
To be in a pickle,<b>Meaning:</b> To be in a difficult or unpleasant situation. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the 16th century; being 'mixed up' or 'preserved' like vegetables in vinegar. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I forgot my wallet and my car is out of gas—I'm in a bit of a pickle.
To cost a fortune,<b>Meaning:</b> To be very expensive. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A 'fortune' is a massive amount of wealth. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> That diamond ring must have cost a fortune.
To have a change of heart,"<b>Meaning:</b> To change your opinion or decision. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> The heart is seen as the center of decision-making and feelings. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I wasn't going to go to the party, but I had a change of heart."
To kill two birds with one stone,<b>Meaning:</b> To achieve two things with a single action. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the 17th century; a metaphor for efficiency. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I can drop the kids at school on my way to work and kill two birds with one stone.
To play it safe,"<b>Meaning:</b> To avoid risks and act carefully. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A standard advice for caution. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I think we should play it safe and take the umbrella, just in case."
To pull someone's leg,<b>Meaning:</b> To joke with someone or trick them in a playful way. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Possibly from the way thieves used to trip people to rob them. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Don't believe him; he's just pulling your leg.
To put someone on the spot,"<b>Meaning:</b> To ask someone a difficult question or put them in a difficult situation in front of others. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for forcing someone to stand in a 'spotlight.' <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I didn't mean to put you on the spot, but we need an answer now."
To sit on the fence,<b>Meaning:</b> To avoid making a decision or choosing a side in an argument. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A person sitting on a fence is not in either of the two fields on either side. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> You can't sit on the fence forever; you have to pick a side.
To spill the beans,"<b>Meaning:</b> To reveal a secret. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Ancient Greeks used beans to vote secretly; spilling them revealed the results. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> We were going to surprise her, but Tim spilled the beans."
To take someone under your wing,<b>Meaning:</b> To protect and guide someone who has less experience. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for a mother bird protecting her chicks. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The senior manager took the new intern under her wing.
To turn a blind eye,<b>Meaning:</b> To ignore something that you know is wrong. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Admiral Nelson supposedly held his telescope to his blind eye so he wouldn't 'see' a signal to retreat. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The teacher turned a blind eye to the students whispering.
To walk on eggshells,<b>Meaning:</b> To be very careful about what you say or do around someone to avoid upsetting them. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal image of how carefully you would have to move to avoid breaking fragile eggs. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Everyone in the office is walking on eggshells because the boss is in a bad mood.
Top-notch,<b>Meaning:</b> Excellent; of the highest quality. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From competitive games where the 'top notch' on a scoring stick represented the highest score. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The service at that hotel is absolutely top-notch.
Trial and error,<b>Meaning:</b> Trying different methods until you find the one that works. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A basic method of problem-solving. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I learned how to use the software through trial and error.
True colors,"<b>Meaning:</b> A person's real character or intentions. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> See 'Show your true colors.' <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He seemed nice at first, but he showed his true colors when he got angry."
Two cents,"<b>Meaning:</b> Your opinion about something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the 19th century; the idea that an opinion is worth very little. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> If you want my two cents, I think you should buy the red one."
Up to speed,<b>Meaning:</b> Having all the latest information about something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From engines reaching their required operating speed. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Give me a few minutes to get up to speed on the new project.
Upper hand,<b>Meaning:</b> An advantage or a position of control. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From an old game of 'hand-over-hand' on a stick or bat to see who goes first. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Our team has the upper hand because the other team is missing their best player.
Upset the apple cart,"<b>Meaning:</b> To ruin someone's plans or a stable situation. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal image of knocking over a cart full of apples. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> We had everything planned, but his resignation really upset the apple cart."
Wait for the dust to settle,<b>Meaning:</b> To wait for a situation to become calm or clear before taking action. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for waiting for the dirt kicked up by a fight or explosion to land. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Let's wait for the dust to settle after the merger before we make any changes.
Wake-up call,<b>Meaning:</b> An event that makes you realize you need to change something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From hotels providing a telephone call to wake guests up. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> His heart attack was a real wake-up call to start exercising.
Walk on air,<b>Meaning:</b> To feel extremely happy. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for feeling so light with joy that you don't touch the ground. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I've been walking on air since I got my promotion.
Whole nine yards,"<b>Meaning:</b> Everything; the entire amount. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Disputed; possibly from the length of WWII ammunition belts or fabric for kilts. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I want the full package—the insurance, the warranty, the whole nine yards."
With a grain of salt,"<b>Meaning:</b> To not take something too seriously or literally. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> See 'Take with a grain of salt.' <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He exaggerates a lot, so take his stories with a grain of salt."
Wrong side of the bed,<b>Meaning:</b> To be in a bad mood for no particular reason. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> See 'Get up on the wrong side of the bed.' <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Don't talk to her today; she got up on the wrong side of the bed.
You reap what you sow,<b>Meaning:</b> You will eventually face the consequences of your actions. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the Bible (Galatians 6:7). <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He was lazy all year and failed his exams. You reap what you sow.
All bark and no bite,<b>Meaning:</b> Someone who acts tough or threatening but is actually harmless. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal description of a dog that barks loudly but never attacks. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Don't be afraid of the manager; he's all bark and no bite.
In the blink of an eye,<b>Meaning:</b> Extremely quickly. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal description of how fast a human eyelid moves. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The accident happened in the blink of an eye.
In the long run,"<b>Meaning:</b> Over a long period of time; eventually. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From long-distance racing; the final result matters more than the initial sprint. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> It seems expensive now, but it will save us money in the long run."
In the loop,<b>Meaning:</b> Part of a group that is kept informed about something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Refers to a communication 'loop' where information circulates. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Please keep me in the loop regarding any changes to the schedule.
In the nick of time,<b>Meaning:</b> At the very last possible moment. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A 'nick' was a small notch cut into a stick to keep track of time or scores. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The ambulance arrived in the nick of time.
Inside out,<b>Meaning:</b> Knowing something thoroughly. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Like knowing a piece of clothing so well you know the seams on the inside as well as the outside. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He’s been a mechanic for 40 years; he knows engines inside out.
Jack of all trades,"<b>Meaning:</b> A person who can do many different types of work. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the 1600s; 'Jack' was a generic name for a common man. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He can fix cars, paint houses, and garden; he’s a real jack of all trades."
Keep your shirt on,"<b>Meaning:</b> A way of telling someone to remain calm and patient. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Before a fight, men would take off their shirts; keeping it on means staying peaceful. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Keep your shirt on! I’ll be ready in five minutes."
Kicked the bucket,"<b>Meaning:</b> To die. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> One theory involves a person standing on a bucket to hang themselves, then 'kicking' it away. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Our old neighbor finally kicked the bucket at age 98."
Kill the messenger,"<b>Meaning:</b> To blame the person who brings bad news. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Ancient practice where kings would execute messengers bringing news of defeat. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Don't kill the messenger, but your car has been towed."
Larger than life,<b>Meaning:</b> Someone who attracts a lot of attention because they are more exciting than average people. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Describing something that exceeds normal proportions. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> My uncle was a larger-than-life character who always had the best stories.
Laugh all the way to the bank,"<b>Meaning:</b> To make a lot of money from something, especially if others criticized it. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Attributed to the pianist Liberace. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Critics hated the movie, but it was a huge hit; the director is laughing all the way to the bank."
Left in the lurch,<b>Meaning:</b> Abandoned in a difficult situation. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From an old French game similar to backgammon called 'lourche.' <br><br> <b>Example:</b> My partner quit right before the deadline and left me in the lurch.
Live and let live,"<b>Meaning:</b> To accept other people's opinions and behavior even if they are different from yours. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A 17th-century proverb. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I don't agree with their lifestyle, but live and let live, I guess."
Low-hanging fruit,<b>Meaning:</b> The easiest tasks or goals to achieve. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Fruit on the bottom branches of a tree is easiest to pick. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Let's focus on the low-hanging fruit first to get some quick wins.
Middle of the road,"<b>Meaning:</b> Ordinary; not extreme or controversial. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Avoiding the 'ditches' or 'gutters' on either side of a path. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Their music is very middle of the road; it's not great, but it's not bad."
Miss the mark,<b>Meaning:</b> To fail to achieve a result or be incorrect. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From archery or shooting; failing to hit the target. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> His prediction about the election completely missed the mark.
Monday morning quarterback,<b>Meaning:</b> Someone who criticizes or judges a situation after it has already happened. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Fans who watch American football on Sunday and criticize the plays on Monday. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> It's easy to be a Monday morning quarterback and say what we should have done.
Neither here nor there,<b>Meaning:</b> Irrelevant or unimportant. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Something that doesn't fit into any specific category of importance. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Whether I like the color or not is neither here nor there; we have to buy it.
New kid on the block,"<b>Meaning:</b> Someone who has just joined a group or moved to a new place. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal description of a child moving to a new neighborhood. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> As the new kid on the block, I had to work hard to prove myself."
No strings attached,<b>Meaning:</b> An offer that has no hidden conditions or requirements. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likely from the textile industry or puppetry; no 'strings' to control you. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I’ll give you the money as a gift—no strings attached.
Not a spark of truth,<b>Meaning:</b> Completely false. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A 'spark' is the smallest bit of light; its absence means total darkness (lies). <br><br> <b>Example:</b> There wasn't a spark of truth in his story about the accident.
Off the beaten path,<b>Meaning:</b> In a place where few people go; unusual. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal path that hasn't been 'beaten' or flattened by many footsteps. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> We found a great little restaurant off the beaten path.
Off the record,"<b>Meaning:</b> Information that is not intended to be made public. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From journalism; information that cannot be officially 'recorded' or quoted. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Off the record, I think the manager is going to resign."
Out of the frying pan and into the fire,<b>Meaning:</b> Going from a bad situation to an even worse one. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> First used in the 1500s. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I quit my stressful job only to find my new one is even worse; out of the frying pan and into the fire.
Out of the woods,"<b>Meaning:</b> No longer in danger or difficulty. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for being lost in a dark, dangerous forest and finally finding the exit. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The surgery was successful, but the patient isn't out of the woods yet."
Over my dead body,<b>Meaning:</b> I will never allow this to happen. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A dramatic way to say you would rather die than see something occur. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> You’re selling my car? Over my dead body!
Paddle your own canoe,"<b>Meaning:</b> To be independent and take care of yourself. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> An American idiom from the 19th century. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Now that you're 18, it's time to learn how to paddle your own canoe."
Paint the town red,<b>Meaning:</b> To go out and celebrate wildly. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Possibly from an 1837 incident where a group of men literally painted buildings red. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> It’s my birthday; let’s go out and paint the town red!
Pandora's box,<b>Meaning:</b> A source of many unforeseen troubles. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Greek mythology; Pandora opened a box that released all the evils into the world. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Investigation into the minor theft opened a Pandora's box of corruption.
Penny-pincher,<b>Meaning:</b> A person who is very careful with money; a stingy person. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for someone holding onto their coins so tightly they 'pinch' them. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> My boss is such a penny-pincher that he won't even buy new pens for the office.
Play devil's advocate,"<b>Meaning:</b> To argue against an idea just to test its strength or provoke discussion. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> An official position in the Catholic Church whose job was to find flaws in evidence for sainthood. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I agree with you, but let me play devil's advocate for a moment."
Point of no return,"<b>Meaning:</b> The stage in a process where it is impossible to go back. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From aviation; the point on a flight where a plane doesn't have enough fuel to return to its start. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Once we sign this contract, we’ve reached the point of no return."
Pull a fast one,<b>Meaning:</b> To trick or deceive someone. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likely from card games or magic tricks where fast hand movements hide the truth. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He tried to pull a fast one by charging me double the price.
Pull your weight,"<b>Meaning:</b> To do your fair share of work in a group. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From rowing; each person must pull their oar with enough strength to move the boat's weight. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> If you don't start pulling your weight, the team will fail."
Rally the troops,<b>Meaning:</b> To encourage and organize people to work together. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Military; bringing soldiers together to prepare for battle. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> We need to rally the troops if we want to finish this project by Friday.
Rough around the edges,"<b>Meaning:</b> Having good qualities but lacking polish or refinement. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Refers to a raw diamond or a piece of wood that hasn't been sanded smooth. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He’s a great worker, but his manners are a bit rough around the edges."
Rub someone the wrong way,"<b>Meaning:</b> To annoy or irritate someone. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Refers to petting a cat's fur in the wrong direction, which makes the cat angry. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I don't know why, but his voice just rubs me the wrong way."
Run circles around someone,<b>Meaning:</b> To be much better or faster than someone else. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for having so much energy or skill that you can circle your opponent while they struggle. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> She can run circles around the other students when it comes to math.
Save for a rainy day,<b>Meaning:</b> To save money for a time in the future when you might need it unexpectedly. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A 'rainy day' represents a time of difficulty when you cannot work outside. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I put $50 from every paycheck into a savings account to save for a rainy day.
Scrape the bottom of the barrel,"<b>Meaning:</b> To use the worst people or things because there is nothing better left. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> When food is running low, you have to scrape the very last (often lower quality) bits from the bottom. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> They really scraped the bottom of the barrel when they hired him."
See red,<b>Meaning:</b> To become very angry. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From bullfighting; bulls were thought to be angered by the color red (though they are actually colorblind). <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I saw red when I found out he had lied to me.
Shoulder to cry on,<b>Meaning:</b> Someone who listens to your problems and gives you sympathy. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A physical metaphor for leaning on someone while weeping. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> She was a great friend and always provided a shoulder to cry on.
Sick and tired,<b>Meaning:</b> Very annoyed and frustrated with something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> An exaggeration of emotional fatigue. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I'm sick and tired of this cold weather.
Silver bullet,<b>Meaning:</b> A simple and magical solution to a complicated problem. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From folklore; the only way to kill a werewolf was with a silver bullet. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> There is no silver bullet for the country's economic problems.
Skeleton staff,"<b>Meaning:</b> The smallest number of people needed to keep a business or organization running. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A 'skeleton' is the basic framework of a body without any 'extra' parts. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The office is open during the holidays, but only with a skeleton staff."
Skin in the game,<b>Meaning:</b> Having a personal investment or risk in an outcome. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Popularized by Warren Buffett; 'skin' refers to one's own money or self. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I’m much more careful with this project now that I have skin in the game.
Sling mud,<b>Meaning:</b> To make insulting or damaging remarks about someone to ruin their reputation. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A literal image of throwing dirt at someone's clean clothes. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The two candidates spent the whole debate slinging mud at each other.
Smooth over,<b>Meaning:</b> To make a problem or disagreement seem less serious. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for sanding down a rough surface. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I tried to smooth over the argument between my two friends.
Sods law,"<b>Meaning:</b> The idea that if something can go wrong, it will. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> British version of Murphy's Law. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> It’s Sods law that it started raining the moment I left my umbrella at home."
Bridge the gap,<b>Meaning:</b> To reduce the differences between two things or groups. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Engineering; building a structure to connect two sides of a divide. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> This new scholarship is designed to bridge the gap between rich and poor students.
Brush up on,<b>Meaning:</b> To refresh one's knowledge of something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likely from cleaning or 'brushing' off dust from an old object to make it usable again. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I need to brush up on my French before our trip to Paris.
Burn the bridge behind you,"<b>Meaning:</b> To act in a way that makes it impossible to return to a previous state. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Military; destroying a bridge after crossing so the enemy cannot follow and you cannot retreat. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He insulted his boss on the way out, effectively burning the bridge behind him."
By a landslide,<b>Meaning:</b> To win an election or competition by a very large margin. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Comparing a massive victory to the overwhelming force of falling earth and rock. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The mayor was re-elected by a landslide.
Call it a night,"<b>Meaning:</b> To stop an activity and go to bed. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Similar to 'call it a day,' but specifically for evening activities. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> It’s 11 PM and I'm tired; let's call it a night."
Can't make heads or tails of it,"<b>Meaning:</b> To be completely unable to understand something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the two sides of a coin; if you can't see either side, you don't know what you have. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I've read this manual three times, but I can't make heads or tails of it."
Carry a tune,"<b>Meaning:</b> To be able to sing melody accurately. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for 'holding' the notes of a song in the correct place. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He’s a nice guy, but he really can't carry a tune."
Catch-22,"<b>Meaning:</b> A paradoxical situation from which an individual cannot escape because of contradictory rules. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From Joseph Heller’s 1961 novel; a pilot can be grounded if he's crazy, but asking to be grounded proves he's sane. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I can't get a job without experience, but I can't get experience without a job—it's a Catch-22."
Day in the sun,"<b>Meaning:</b> A period of success, popularity, or fame. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for standing in the light and warmth of public attention. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> After years of training, the athlete finally had her day in the sun."
Dead in the water,"<b>Meaning:</b> A plan or project that has failed and has no chance of succeeding. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Nautical; a sailing ship that cannot move because there is no wind. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Without the new investment, the project is dead in the water."
Dead to the world,<b>Meaning:</b> Fast asleep or unconscious. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A person who is so deeply asleep they are completely unaware of their surroundings. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He’s been working for 20 hours; he’s dead to the world right now.
Dog-eat-dog world,"<b>Meaning:</b> A situation of fierce competition where people will hurt each other to succeed. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From a Latin proverb; usually 'dog does not eat dog,' which was later inverted to describe extreme ruthlessness. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Business can be a dog-eat-dog world."
Don't put words in my mouth,"<b>Meaning:</b> Don't claim that I said something when I didn't. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for someone trying to control or falsify another's speech. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I said the movie was long, not that it was bad; don't put words in my mouth."
Double take,<b>Meaning:</b> Looking at someone or something a second time because you are surprised by what you saw. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From film and theater; a delayed reaction for comedic effect. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I did a double take when I saw him walking down the street in a tuxedo.
Dry run,<b>Meaning:</b> A rehearsal or practice session before the real event. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likely from fire departments practicing without actually using water (staying 'dry'). <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Let's do a dry run of the presentation before the meeting tomorrow.
Egg on your face,<b>Meaning:</b> To be embarrassed because of a mistake you made. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likely from people throwing eggs at bad performers in a theater. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He’s going to have egg on his face when he finds out he sent the email to the wrong person.
Explore every avenue,<b>Meaning:</b> To try every possible way to achieve something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for searching every street (avenue) in a city. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> We must explore every avenue to find a cure for this disease.
Feel it in your bones,<b>Meaning:</b> To have a strong intuition or feeling about something. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Refers to the way old injuries or arthritis can flare up when the weather changes. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I just feel it in my bones that something good is going to happen today.
Field day,"<b>Meaning:</b> A time of great enjoyment or success, often at someone else's expense. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From military maneuvers performed in an open field for review. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The newspapers had a field day with the politician's latest scandal."
Find your feet,"<b>Meaning:</b> To become confident and comfortable in a new situation. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for a baby learning to walk or a sailor getting used to a moving ship. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> It took a few weeks, but I’m finally finding my feet in my new job."
Finger in every pie,"<b>Meaning:</b> Being involved in many different activities or businesses, often in an annoying way. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A metaphor for someone who can't resist touching everything. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> He’s very powerful in this town; he has a finger in every pie."
First things first,"<b>Meaning:</b> Do the most important things before anything else. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A simple prioritization rule. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I know you want to see the house, but first things first: we need to get the keys."
Fit to be tied,<b>Meaning:</b> Extremely angry or upset. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From the 19th century; someone so furious they had to be physically restrained (tied up). <br><br> <b>Example:</b> My mother was fit to be tied when she saw the mess in the kitchen.
Follow your gut,"<b>Meaning:</b> To make a decision based on your feelings or intuition rather than logic. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> The 'gut' (intestines) is often where people feel a physical reaction to stress or truth. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I didn't have any proof he was lying, so I just followed my gut."
For the birds,"<b>Meaning:</b> Worthless, ridiculous, or uninteresting. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likely from the idea that only birds would find seeds in horse manure interesting. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> This new television show is for the birds."
Freudian slip,"<b>Meaning:</b> An unintentional mistake in speech that is thought to reveal a person's true feelings. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Named after Sigmund Freud, the founder of psychoanalysis. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> She called her new boyfriend by her ex-husband's name; it was a classic Freudian slip."
From rags to riches,<b>Meaning:</b> Going from being very poor to being very wealthy. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A common theme in folklore and literature (like Cinderella). <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The billionaire’s story is a classic case of from rags to riches.
From the bottom of my heart,<b>Meaning:</b> With sincere and deep feeling. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> The deepest part of the heart is seen as the most honest. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I want to thank you from the bottom of my heart for your help.
Full of hot air,<b>Meaning:</b> Talking a lot without saying anything important or true. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> Likening a person's speech to the useless steam or air in a balloon. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Don't listen to him; he’s just full of hot air.
Green light,<b>Meaning:</b> Permission to start a project or activity. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From traffic signals where a green light means you can proceed. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> The boss finally gave us the green light to start the new campaign.
Haste makes waste,"<b>Meaning:</b> If you do something too quickly, you will make mistakes and waste time or resources. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> A proverb from the 14th century. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> Slow down and check your work; haste makes waste."
Have a bone to pick with someone,<b>Meaning:</b> To have a complaint or grievance that you want to discuss. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From a dog chewing on a bone until every scrap of meat is gone. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> I have a bone to pick with you about the way you spoke to me yesterday.
Hit the jackpot,"<b>Meaning:</b> To have a sudden, great success or to win a lot of money. <br><br> <b>Origin:</b> From slot machines or poker. <br><br> <b>Example:</b> She really hit the jackpot when she found that old painting at the garage sale."
A Bit Much	<b>Bengali:</b> একটু বেশি, অত্যধিক<br><b>English:</b> Too much; excessive<br><b>Example:</b> His constant complaining is a bit much - we get it, you're unhappy.	
A Busy Bee	<b>Bengali:</b> একজন ব্যস্ত, সক্রিয় ব্যক্তি যে দ্রুত এক কাজ থেকে আরেক কাজে চলে যায়<br><b>English:</b> A busy, active person who moves quickly from one task to another<br><b>Example:</b> Sarah is such a busy bee - she's already finished three projects this week.	
A Cat Has Nine Lives	<b>Bengali:</b> বিড়ালের নয়টি জীবন আছে, বিপদ থেকে বেঁচে যাওয়ার ক্ষমতা<br><b>English:</b> The ability to survive danger or bounce back from misfortune<br><b>Example:</b> After surviving three car accidents, John jokes that he has nine lives like a cat.	
A Cold Fish	<b>Bengali:</b> যে ব্যক্তি আবেগ দ্বারা প্রভাবিত হয় না, কঠোর ও নিষ্ঠুর<br><b>English:</b> A person who is unemotional, harsh and cruel<br><b>Example:</b> The new manager is such a cold fish - he never shows any emotion or sympathy.	
A Cut Above	<b>Bengali:</b> সামান্য ভাল, উন্নত মানের<br><b>English:</b> Slightly better, of superior quality<br><b>Example:</b> This restaurant is a cut above the usual fast food places in the area.	
A Cut Below	<b>Bengali:</b> নিম্নমানের, কিছুটা খারাপ<br><b>English:</b> Of inferior quality, somewhat worse<br><b>Example:</b> The service at this hotel is a cut below what I expected for the price.	
A Few Sandwiches Short Of A Picnic	<b>Bengali:</b> অস্বাভাবিকভাবে বোকা, পাগল<br><b>English:</b> Unusually stupid or crazy<br><b>Example:</b> I think our neighbor is a few sandwiches short of a picnic - he talks to his garden gnomes.	
A Home Bird	<b>Bengali:</b> যে তার সামাজিক ও অবসর সময় ঘরে কাটাতে পছন্দ করে<br><b>English:</b> Someone who prefers to spend their social and leisure time at home<br><b>Example:</b> Unlike her party-loving sister, Mary is a home bird who enjoys quiet evenings.	
A Leg Up	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি সুবিধা, সহায়তা<br><b>English:</b> An advantage or assistance<br><b>Example:</b> Having a degree from Harvard gave him a leg up in the job market.	
A Little from Column A, a Little from Column B	<b>Bengali:</b> বিভিন্ন ধারণা থেকে কিছু নিয়ে একটি পদক্ষেপ<br><b>English:</b> Taking some elements from different ideas or approaches<br><b>Example:</b> Our solution was a little from column A, a little from column B - combining both strategies.	
A Million and One	<b>Bengali:</b> অনেক, প্রচুর<br><b>English:</b> Very many, a large number<br><b>Example:</b> She has a million and one excuses for being late to work.	
A Notch Above	<b>Bengali:</b> উচ্চমানের, উন্নত<br><b>English:</b> Of higher quality, superior<br><b>Example:</b> This hotel is definitely a notch above the competition in terms of service.	
A Picture Is Worth a Thousand Words	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি চিত্র হাজার শব্দের সমান<br><b>English:</b> An image can convey more than lengthy descriptions<br><b>Example:</b> Instead of explaining the damage, she just showed them the photo - a picture is worth a thousand words.	
A Second Bite At The Cherry	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু করার দ্বিতীয় সুযোগ<br><b>English:</b> A second chance to do something<br><b>Example:</b> After failing the exam, he was grateful to get a second bite at the cherry.	
A Sight for Sore Eyes	<b>Bengali:</b> এমন কেউ যাকে দেখে আনন্দিত হওয়া যায়<br><b>English:</b> Someone pleasant to see<br><b>Example:</b> After being away for months, seeing my family was a sight for sore eyes.	
A Sitting Duck	<b>Bengali:</b> দুর্বল অবস্থানে থাকা ব্যক্তি বা বস্তু<br><b>English:</b> A person or thing in a vulnerable position<br><b>Example:</b> Without security, the embassy was a sitting duck for terrorist attacks.	
A Tall Order	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি কঠিন কাজ<br><b>English:</b> A difficult task<br><b>Example:</b> Finishing the project in one week is a tall order, but we'll try.	
About To	<b>Bengali:</b> ঘটতে চলেছে, আসন্ন<br><b>English:</b> Going to happen soon, imminent<br><b>Example:</b> The movie is about to start, so we should find our seats.	
Above Board	<b>Bengali:</b> খোলামেলা, প্রতারণা ছাড়া, সততার সাথে<br><b>English:</b> Open, honest, without deception<br><b>Example:</b> All our business dealings are completely above board.	
Above The Law	<b>Bengali:</b> আইনের উর্ধ্বে, আইনের বাইরে<br><b>English:</b> Not subject to legal restrictions<br><b>Example:</b> No one is above the law, not even the president.	
Above The Salt	<b>Bengali:</b> উচ্চ মর্যাদার বা সম্মানের<br><b>English:</b> Of high status or honor<br><b>Example:</b> In medieval times, sitting above the salt indicated noble status.	
Above Water	<b>Bengali:</b> চরম অসুবিধায় নেই, বিশেষত আর্থিকভাবে<br><b>English:</b> Not in extreme difficulty, especially financially<br><b>Example:</b> Despite the recession, the company managed to stay above water.	
According To Hoyle	<b>Bengali:</b> যথাযথভাবে, স্থাপিত নিয়ম অনুসারে<br><b>English:</b> Properly, according to established rules<br><b>Example:</b> We played poker according to Hoyle - no variations or house rules.	
Acknowledge The Corn	<b>Bengali:</b> ভুল স্বীকার করা, নিজের ত্রুটি নির্দেশ করা<br><b>English:</b> To admit a mistake or acknowledge one's faults<br><b>Example:</b> After the evidence was presented, he had to acknowledge the corn.	
Across The Board	<b>Bengali:</b> সব ক্ষেত্রে, সবার জন্য<br><b>English:</b> In all areas, for everyone<br><b>Example:</b> The company implemented salary increases across the board.	
Act High and Mighty	<b>Bengali:</b> অহংকারী হওয়া, নিজেকে অন্যদের চেয়ে ভাল মনে করা<br><b>English:</b> To be arrogant, to think oneself better than others<br><b>Example:</b> Don't act high and mighty just because you got promoted.	
Act One's Age	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিপক্ব হওয়া, শিশুসুলভ আচরণ না করা<br><b>English:</b> To behave maturely, not childishly<br><b>Example:</b> You're thirty years old - act your age and stop playing pranks.	
Actions Speak Louder Than Words	<b>Bengali:</b> কথার চেয়ে কাজ বেশি গুরুত্বপূর্ণ<br><b>English:</b> What you do is more important than what you say<br><b>Example:</b> He promised to help, but actions speak louder than words.	
Add Insult To Injury	<b>Bengali:</b> পরাজয়ের সাথে অপমান যোগ করা<br><b>English:</b> To make a bad situation even worse<br><b>Example:</b> Not only did they fire him, but they also asked him to train his replacement - adding insult to injury.	
After The Fact	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব দেরিতে, কিছু সম্পূর্ণ হওয়ার পর<br><b>English:</b> Too late, after something is completed<br><b>Example:</b> You can't change the contract after the fact - it's already signed.	
After The Lord Mayor's Show	<b>Bengali:</b> চিত্তাকর্ষক কিছুর পর নিরস লাগা<br><b>English:</b> Feeling anticlimactic after something impressive<br><b>Example:</b> After the spectacular opening ceremony, the regular events felt like after the Lord Mayor's show.	
Against The Clock	<b>Bengali:</b> সময়সীমা মেনে চলতে বাধ্য<br><b>English:</b> Under time pressure, racing against a deadline<br><b>Example:</b> We're working against the clock to finish this project by Friday.	
Age Before Beauty	<b>Bengali:</b> বয়স্কদের আগে যাওয়ার সুযোগ দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Giving older people priority<br><b>Example:</b> After you, grandmother - age before beauty.	
Agree To Disagree	<b>Bengali:</b> মতবিরোধ মেনে নেওয়া বা পাশে রাখা<br><b>English:</b> To accept disagreement and move on<br><b>Example:</b> We'll never see eye to eye on politics, so let's agree to disagree.	
Agreement In Principle	<b>Bengali:</b> নীতিগতভাবে সম্মত হওয়া যেখানে সব বিস্তারিত ঠিক করা হয়নি<br><b>English:</b> General agreement where details haven't been worked out<br><b>Example:</b> We have an agreement in principle, but the lawyers need to finalize the terms.	
Aha Moment	<b>Bengali:</b> হঠাৎ অনুধাবন, হঠাৎ বুঝে ওঠা<br><b>English:</b> Sudden realization or understanding<br><b>Example:</b> I had an aha moment when I finally understood the math problem.	
Ahead Of One's Time	<b>Bengali:</b> সাধারণ প্রচলনের আগে ধারণা প্রদান, অত্যন্ত সৃজনশীল<br><b>English:</b> Having ideas before they become commonly accepted<br><b>Example:</b> Leonardo da Vinci was truly ahead of his time with his inventions.	
Ahead Of The Curve	<b>Bengali:</b> উদ্ভাবনী, অন্যদের আগে নতুন ধারণা প্রদান<br><b>English:</b> Innovative, ahead of others in new ideas<br><b>Example:</b> Apple has always been ahead of the curve in smartphone design.	
Ahead Of The Game	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রত্যাশিত গতির চেয়ে দ্রুত অগ্রগতি<br><b>English:</b> Making faster progress than expected<br><b>Example:</b> By finishing the report early, we're ahead of the game for once.	
Airy Fairy	<b>Bengali:</b> অযৌক্তিক, অবাস্তব<br><b>English:</b> Unrealistic or impractical<br><b>Example:</b> His business plan is too airy fairy - it lacks concrete details.	
Alive and Kicking	<b>Bengali:</b> স্বাস্থ্য সমস্যা সত্ত্বেও ভাল স্বাস্থ্যে<br><b>English:</b> In good health despite health issues<br><b>Example:</b> Despite being ninety, my grandfather is still alive and kicking.	
All Dressed Up And Nowhere To Go	<b>Bengali:</b> কোনো অনুষ্ঠানের জন্য প্রস্তুত কিন্তু অনুষ্ঠান হলো না<br><b>English:</b> Ready for an event that gets cancelled<br><b>Example:</b> When the party was cancelled, I was all dressed up and nowhere to go.	
All Hands on Deck	<b>Bengali:</b> সবাইকে সাহায্য করতে হবে<br><b>English:</b> Everyone needs to help<br><b>Example:</b> With the deadline approaching, it's all hands on deck to finish the project.	
All Hat And No Cattle	<b>Bengali:</b> দম্ভপূর্ণ, অভিমানী কিন্তু প্রকৃত গুণাবলী নেই<br><b>English:</b> Boastful but lacking real substance or ability<br><b>Example:</b> The new manager is all hat and no cattle - lots of talk but no results.	
All Hell Breaks Loose	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিস্থিতি বিশৃঙ্খল হয়ে ওঠে<br><b>English:</b> Chaos erupts<br><b>Example:</b> When the fire alarm went off during the meeting, all hell broke loose.	
"All In Good Time	""<b>Bengali:</b> অবশেষে", ভবিষ্যতে আরও অনুকূল সময়ে<br><b>English:</b> Eventually, at a more favorable time in the future<br><b>Example:</b> You'll get your promotion all in good time - just be patient.
Babe In The Woods	<b>Bengali:</b> নিষ্পাপ, সরল ব্যক্তি<br><b>English:</b> An innocent, naive person<br><b>Example:</b> In the corporate world, he's just a babe in the woods.	
Babe Magnet	<b>Bengali:</b> যে পুরুষের প্রতি নারীরা আকৃষ্ট হয়<br><b>English:</b> A man who attracts women<br><b>Example:</b> With his charm and good looks, he's a real babe magnet.	
Back And Forth	<b>Bengali:</b> কথোপকথন, আলোচনা<br><b>English:</b> Conversation, discussion<br><b>Example:</b> The negotiations went back and forth for hours.

Back Forty	<b>Bengali:</b> দুর্গম, অগম্য ভূমি<br><b>English:</b> Remote, inaccessible land<br><b>Example:</b> He built his cabin in the back forty where no one could find him.	
Back Of Beyond	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি প্রত্যন্ত স্থান<br><b>English:</b> A very remote place<br><b>Example:</b> They live in the back of beyond, miles from civilization.	
Back Office	<b>Bengali:</b> ব্যবসার সহায়ক সেবা<br><b>English:</b> Support services of a business<br><b>Example:</b> While sales teams meet clients, back office staff handle paperwork.	
Back in the Day	<b>Bengali:</b> আগের দিনে, যখন আমি ছোট ছিলাম<br><b>English:</b> In the past, when I was younger<br><b>Example:</b> Back in the day, we didn't have smartphones.	
Back on One's Feet	<b>Bengali:</b> শারীরিকভাবে আবার সুস্থ হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Physically recovered again<br><b>Example:</b> After the surgery, it took months to get back on his feet.

Bad Apple	<b>Bengali:</b> অসন্তুষ্ট, সমস্যা সৃষ্টিকারী বা অসৎ ব্যক্তি<br><b>English:</b> A troublesome or dishonest person<br><b>Example:</b> One bad apple in the team can ruin the whole project.	
Bad Taste In One's Mouth	<b>Bengali:</b> অস্বস্তি, কিছু ভুল আছে এমন অনুভূতি<br><b>English:</b> Discomfort, feeling that something is wrong<br><b>Example:</b> The way they fired him left a bad taste in my mouth.	
Bag of Tricks	<b>Bengali:</b> পদ্ধতি বা সম্পদের সংগ্রহ<br><b>English:</b> Collection of methods or resources<br><b>Example:</b> As a teacher, she has a whole bag of tricks to keep students engaged.
