Until You're Blue in the Face	<b>Bengali:</b> দীর্ঘ সময় ধরে ফলাফল ছাড়া<br><b>English:</b> For a long time with no results<br><b>Example:</b> You can complain until you're blue in the face, but nothing will change.	
Up a Creek	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব খারাপ পরিস্থিতিতে<br><b>English:</b> In a very bad situation<br><b>Example:</b> Without a car, we're really up a creek.	
Up in Arms	<b>Bengali:</b> রাগান্বিত, প্রতিবাদী<br><b>English:</b> Angry, protesting (usually said of a group)<br><b>Example:</b> The residents are up in arms about the new highway.	
Upset the Apple Cart	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু অগোছালো বা নষ্ট করা<br><b>English:</b> To disorganize or spoil something, especially an established arrangement or plan<br><b>Example:</b> Don't upset the apple cart by changing the schedule now.	
Use One's Head	<b>Bengali:</b> চিন্তা করা, সাধারণ জ্ঞান ব্যবহার করা<br><b>English:</b> To think, to have common sense<br><b>Example:</b> Use your head - that plan will never work.	
Vale of Tears	<b>Bengali:</b> জীবনের দুঃখ-কষ্ট<br><b>English:</b> The world in general, envisioned as a sad place; the tribulations of life<br><b>Example:</b> Life in this vale of tears can be difficult.	
Victory Lap	<b>Bengali:</b> বিজয়ের পর প্রকাশ্য উপস্থিতি<br><b>English:</b> Visible public appearances after a victory or accomplishment<br><b>Example:</b> After winning the election, she took a victory lap through the district.	
Virgin Territory	<b>Bengali:</b> যা কখনো অন্বেষণ করা হয়নি<br><b>English:</b> Something that has never been explored, physically or intellectually<br><b>Example:</b> This research area is virgin territory for scientists.	
Vote with One's Feet	<b>Bengali:</b> অসন্তুষ্টি প্রকাশের জন্য শারীরিকভাবে চলে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To physically depart from something as a way of showing disapproval<br><b>Example:</b> When the company cut benefits, many employees voted with their feet.	
Waiting in the Wings	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রস্তুত অবস্থায় অপেক্ষা করা, উত্তরাধিকারী হওয়ার জন্য প্রস্তুত<br><b>English:</b> Ready to assume responsibilities but not yet active, ready to become a successor<br><b>Example:</b> The vice president is waiting in the wings for his chance to lead.	
Wake Up and Smell the Coffee	<b>Bengali:</b> নিজেকে ধোঁকা দেওয়া বন্ধ করো, বাস্তবতা বুঝো<br><b>English:</b> Stop deluding yourself<br><b>Example:</b> Wake up and smell the coffee - she's not interested in you.	
Walk the Plank	<b>Bengali:</b> পদত্যাগ করতে বাধ্য হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Be forced to resign a position<br><b>Example:</b> After the scandal, the CEO was forced to walk the plank.	
Wash Your Hands of (Something)	<b>Bengali:</b> দায়িত্ব নিতে অস্বীকার করা, আর জড়িত না থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Decline to take further responsibility; refuse to be involved with something anymore<br><b>Example:</b> I wash my hands of this whole mess.	
Watering Hole	<b>Bengali:</b> মদের দোকান, বার<br><b>English:</b> A place where alcoholic beverages are served, a bar<br><b>Example:</b> Let's meet at the local watering hole after work.	
Wet Behind the Ears	<b>Bengali:</b> অনভিজ্ঞ, অপরিপক্ব, নতুন<br><b>English:</b> Inexperienced, immature, new to something<br><b>Example:</b> The new intern is still wet behind the ears.	
What Goes Around Comes Around	<b>Bengali:</b> যেমন কর্ম তেমন ফল<br><b>English:</b> The kind of treatment you give to others will eventually return to you; things go in cycles<br><b>Example:</b> He treated his employees badly, and what goes around comes around.	
What's Good for the Goose Is Good for the Gander	<b>Bengali:</b> পুরুষের জন্য যা ঠিক, নারীর জন্যও তা ঠিক<br><b>English:</b> What's OK for a man is OK for a woman, too<br><b>Example:</b> If he can work late, so can she - what's good for the goose is good for the gander.	
When In Doubt, Leave It Out	<b>Bengali:</b> সন্দেহ থাকলে বাদ দিয়ে দাও<br><b>English:</b> When unsure about something, omit it<br><b>Example:</b> When in doubt about that quote, leave it out of your speech.	
When It Rains, It Pours	<b>Bengali:</b> বিপদ একা আসে না<br><b>English:</b> Problems tend to come in groups<br><b>Example:</b> First my car broke down, then I got sick - when it rains, it pours.	
When the Chips Are Down	<b>Bengali:</b> যখন পরিস্থিতি কঠিন হয়ে ওঠে<br><b>English:</b> When a situation becomes urgent or difficult<br><b>Example:</b> When the chips are down, she always comes through.	
Where (When) the Rubber Meets the Road	<b>Bengali:</b> বাস্তবে; যেখানে ধারণা বাস্তব পরীক্ষার মুখোমুখি হয়<br><b>English:</b> In reality; where an idea meets a real-world test<br><b>Example:</b> The theory sounds good, but where the rubber meets the road, it doesn't work.	
Where There's a Will, There's a Way	<b>Bengali:</b> যেখানে ইচ্ছা সেখানে উপায়<br><b>English:</b> If you have a strong desire to accomplish something, you will achieve it even in the face of considerable odds<br><b>Example:</b> She was determined to finish college, and where there's a will, there's a way.	
Where There's Smoke, There's Fire	<b>Bengali:</b> ধোঁয়া দেখলে আগুন আছে বুঝতে হবে<br><b>English:</b> If there is typical evidence of something, the most likely explanation is that it is actually occurring<br><b>Example:</b> Where there's smoke, there's fire - those rumors might be true.	
Whistling Dixie	<b>Bengali:</b> অবাস্তব আশাবাদী হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Being unrealistically optimistic<br><b>Example:</b> If you think the project will finish on time, you're whistling Dixie.	
Who's She, the Cat's Mother?	<b>Bengali:</b> সে নিজেকে কী মনে করে?<br><b>English:</b> Why does she have such a high opinion of herself?<br><b>Example:</b> She wants special treatment? Who's she, the cat's mother?	
With Bells On	<b>Bengali:</b> উৎসাহের সাথে, স্বেচ্ছায় এবং সময়মতো<br><b>English:</b> Eagerly, willingly, and on time<br><b>Example:</b> I'll be at your party with bells on!	
Worn to a Frazzle	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্পূর্ণ ক্লান্ত, শেষ হয়ে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Exhausted, completely worn out<br><b>Example:</b> After the long conference, I was worn to a frazzle.	
Year In, Year Out	<b>Bengali:</b> বছরের পর বছর একইভাবে<br><b>English:</b> Annually without change<br><b>Example:</b> Year in, year out, he follows the same routine.	
You Can Lead a Horse to Water, but You Can't Make It Drink	<b>Bengali:</b> জোর করে কাউকে দিয়ে কিছু করানো যায় না<br><b>English:</b> It's very hard to force someone to do something against his or her will<br><b>Example:</b> I showed him how to study, but you can lead a horse to water, but you can't make it drink.	
You Can't Judge a Book by Its Cover	<b>Bengali:</b> বাহ্যিক চেহারা দেখে মানুষকে বোঝা যায় না<br><b>English:</b> You can't know people (or things) well by their external appearances<br><b>Example:</b> He looks rough, but you can't judge a book by its cover.	
You Snooze, You Lose	<b>Bengali:</b> দেরি করলে সুযোগ হাতছাড়া হয়ে যাবে<br><b>English:</b> If you delay or are not alert, you will miss opportunities<br><b>Example:</b> The tickets sold out in minutes - you snooze, you lose.	
Young at Heart	<b>Bengali:</b> বয়স নির্বিশেষে তরুণ মানসিকতা রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Having a youthful outlook, regardless of age<br><b>Example:</b> At 70, she's still young at heart and loves adventure.	
Your Mileage May Vary	<b>Bengali:</b> তোমার ফলাফল ভিন্ন হতে পারে<br><b>English:</b> You may get different results. This does not necessarily refer to a car, although it may<br><b>Example:</b> This diet worked for me, but your mileage may vary.	
Your Number Is Up	<b>Bengali:</b> তোমার সময় শেষ হয়ে এসেছে<br><b>English:</b> You are going to die (or suffer some bad misfortune or setback)<br><b>Example:</b> When the boss calls you to his office, your number is up.	
Yours Truly	<b>Bengali:</b> আমি<br><b>English:</b> Me<br><b>Example:</b> Who's going to clean this mess? Yours truly, I suppose.	
Step Up One's Game	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতিযোগিতায় উন্নতির চেষ্টা করা<br><b>English:</b> Work to advance to a higher level of a competition<br><b>Example:</b> If you want that promotion, you need to step up your game.	
Step Up to the Plate	<b>Bengali:</b> দায়িত্ব নেওয়ার জন্য প্রস্তুত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Prepare to take action, be the person in a group who takes action<br><b>Example:</b> When the manager quit, someone had to step up to the plate.	
Sticky Wicket	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন পরিস্থিতি<br><b>English:</b> A difficult, tricky situation<br><b>Example:</b> Explaining the layoffs to employees will be a sticky wicket.	
Storm in a Teacup	<b>Bengali:</b> তুচ্ছ বিষয়ে বড় হৈচৈ<br><b>English:</b> A commotion that dies down quickly, about something unimportant<br><b>Example:</b> The controversy over the dress code was a storm in a teacup.	
Stumbling Block	<b>Bengali:</b> বাধা<br><b>English:</b> An obstacle, physical or abstract<br><b>Example:</b> Lack of funding is the main stumbling block to the project.	
Straight Arrow	<b>Bengali:</b> সৎ ও বিশ্বস্ত ব্যক্তি<br><b>English:</b> An honest, trustworthy person<br><b>Example:</b> You can trust him - he's a straight arrow.	
Strain at a Gnat and Swallow a Camel	<b>Bengali:</b> ছোট বিষয়ে হৈচৈ, বড় বিষয় উপেক্ষা<br><b>English:</b> To make a fuss over something unimportant while ignoring larger issues<br><b>Example:</b> Worrying about grammar while ignoring the main argument is straining at a gnat and swallowing a camel.	
Strike A Chord	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিচিত লাগা, মনে পড়া<br><b>English:</b> Used to describe something that is familiar to you, reminds you of something or is connected to you somehow<br><b>Example:</b> Her story about growing up poor struck a chord with me.	
Sweet Dreams!	<b>Bengali:</b> ভালো ঘুম হোক!<br><b>English:</b> Sleep well!<br><b>Example:</b> Good night, honey - sweet dreams!	
Sweeten the Deal	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রস্তাবে আকর্ষণীয় কিছু যোগ করা<br><b>English:</b> Add something to an offer during a negotiation<br><b>Example:</b> To sweeten the deal, they threw in free shipping.	
Sweeten the Pot	<b>Bengali:</b> জয়ের পরিমাণ বাড়ানো<br><b>English:</b> Increase the amount of winnings potentially available in a game of chance, especially poker<br><b>Example:</b> The casino sweetened the pot to attract more players.	
Swim with the Fishes	<b>Bengali:</b> মারা যাওয়া, বিশেষত অপরাধ জগতে<br><b>English:</b> Have been killed, especially with involvement of organized crime<br><b>Example:</b> Cross the mob boss and you'll swim with the fishes.	
Swing for the Fences	<b>Bengali:</b> সর্বোচ্চ অর্জনের চেষ্টা<br><b>English:</b> Attempt to achieve the largest accomplishment possible<br><b>Example:</b> With this new product, we're swinging for the fences.	
Take a Hike	<b>Bengali:</b> চলে যাও<br><b>English:</b> Go away<br><b>Example:</b> When he kept bothering me, I told him to take a hike.	
Take A Powder	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন পরিস্থিতি এড়াতে চলে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To leave, especially in order to avoid a difficult situation<br><b>Example:</b> When the police arrived, the suspect took a powder.	
Take a Rain Check	<b>Bengali:</b> পরে গ্রহণের প্রতিশ্রুতি দিয়ে প্রস্তাব প্রত্যাখ্যান<br><b>English:</b> Decline an invitation but suggest that you'll accept it at a later time<br><b>Example:</b> I can't make dinner tonight, but can I take a rain check?	
Take It on The Chin	<b>Bengali:</b> আক্রমণের শিকার হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Be attacked; suffer an attack<br><b>Example:</b> When the scandal broke, he took it on the chin like a man.	
Take It or Leave It	<b>Bengali:</b> হয় নাও, না হয় ছাড়ো<br><b>English:</b> You must decide now whether you will accept this proposal<br><b>Example:</b> That's my final offer - take it or leave it.	
Take Something with a Pinch of Salt	<b>Bengali:</b> সন্দেহের সাথে গ্রহণ করা<br><b>English:</b> If you take what someone says with a pinch of salt, you do not completely believe it<br><b>Example:</b> Take his fishing stories with a pinch of salt.	
Take the Cake	<b>Bengali:</b> সবচেয়ে চরম উদাহরণ<br><b>English:</b> Be the most extreme instance<br><b>Example:</b> Of all his rude comments, that one takes the cake.	
Take the Fifth	<b>Bengali:</b> উত্তর দিতে অস্বীকার করা<br><b>English:</b> Refuse to answer because answering might incriminate or cause problems for you<br><b>Example:</b> When questioned about the missing money, he took the fifth.	
Take the High Road	<b>Bengali:</b> নৈতিক উচ্চতা বজায় রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Refuse to descend to immoral activities or personal attacks<br><b>Example:</b> Despite the provocation, she took the high road.	
Take The Wind Out of Someone's Sails	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো উৎসাহ কমিয়ে দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To reduce someone's confidence, often by doing something unexpected<br><b>Example:</b> Her criticism took the wind out of his sails.	
Take Your Medicine	<b>Bengali:</b> অপ্রীতিকর কিছু মেনে নেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Accept something unpleasant, for example, punishment, without protesting or complaining<br><b>Example:</b> You made the mistake, now take your medicine.	
Take Your Time	<b>Bengali:</b> তাড়াহুড়ো করো না<br><b>English:</b> Don't hurry, work at a relaxed pace<br><b>Example:</b> Take your time with that decision - it's important.	
Tee Many Martoonies	<b>Bengali:</b> অতিরিক্ত মদ্যপান<br><b>English:</b> Too many martinis, scrambled to suggest drunkenness<br><b>Example:</b> He clearly had tee many martoonies at the party.	
Ten a Penny	<b>Bengali:</b> সাধারণ, সস্তা<br><b>English:</b> Ordinary, inexpensive<br><b>Example:</b> Good programmers aren't ten a penny - they're valuable.	
Test the Waters	<b>Bengali:</b> সাবধানে পরীক্ষা করা<br><b>English:</b> Experiment with something cautiously<br><b>Example:</b> Before investing heavily, let's test the waters with a small amount.	
The Apple Never Falls Far From the Tree	<b>Bengali:</b> পারিবারিক বৈশিষ্ট্য সাধারণত উত্তরাধিকার সূত্রে পাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Family characteristics are usually inherited<br><b>Example:</b> Like father, like son - the apple never falls far from the tree.	
The Cat Is Out of the Bag	<b>Bengali:</b> গোপন কথা ফাঁস হয়ে গেছে<br><b>English:</b> The secret has been revealed<br><b>Example:</b> Well, the cat is out of the bag about the merger.	
The Cherry On the Cake	<b>Bengali:</b> যা কিছুকে নিখুঁত করে তোলে<br><b>English:</b> The final thing that makes something perfect<br><b>Example:</b> Getting promoted was great, but the bonus was the cherry on the cake.	
The Deck Is (The Cards Are): Stacked Against You	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতিকূল পরিস্থিতি বিদ্যমান<br><b>English:</b> Unfavorable conditions exist<br><b>Example:</b> With his background, the deck is stacked against him.	
The Jig Is Up	<b>Bengali:</b> গোপন অবৈধ কার্যকলাপ ফাঁস; তোমার প্রতারণা শেষ<br><b>English:</b> A secret illicit activity has been exposed; your trickery is finished<br><b>Example:</b> When the police arrived, he knew the jig was up.	
The More Things Change, The More They Stay The Same	<b>Bengali:</b> যদিও কিছু নতুন মনে হতে পারে, মূল পরিস্থিতি অপরিবর্তিত<br><b>English:</b> Although something may seem superficially new, it has not altered the basic situation<br><b>Example:</b> New management, same problems - the more things change, the more they stay the same.	
The Powers That Be	<b>Bengali:</b> ক্ষমতাসীন ব্যক্তিরা<br><b>English:</b> People in charge, often used when the speaker does not want to identify them<br><b>Example:</b> The powers that be decided to cancel the project.	
The Time is Ripe	<b>Bengali:</b> উপযুক্ত সময়<br><b>English:</b> If you say that the time is ripe, you mean that it is a suitable point for a particular activity<br><b>Example:</b> The time is ripe for investing in renewable energy.	
The Whole Enchilada	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্পূর্ণ কিছু<br><b>English:</b> All of something<br><b>Example:</b> When I buy a car, I want the whole enchilada - all the options.	
The Whole Shebang	<b>Bengali:</b> সবকিছু, কোনো কিছুর সব অংশ<br><b>English:</b> Everything, all the parts of something<br><b>Example:</b> We're renovating the kitchen - the whole shebang.	
The World Is Your Oyster	<b>Bengali:</b> তোমার অনেক সুযোগ এবং পছন্দ আছে<br><b>English:</b> You have many opportunities and choices<br><b>Example:</b> With your talent and education, the world is your oyster.	
There But For The Grace Of God Go I	<b>Bengali:</b> আমিও সহজেই সেই কাজ করতে পারতাম<br><b>English:</b> I could easily have done what that person did<br><b>Example:</b> Seeing the homeless man, I thought 'there but for the grace of God go I.'	
There's More Than One Way to Skin a Cat	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি লক্ষ্য অর্জনের একাধিক উপায় আছে<br><b>English:</b> There's more than one way of achieving a certain goal<br><b>Example:</b> If that approach doesn't work, don't worry - there's more than one way to skin a cat.	
There's No Such Thing as a Free Lunch	<b>Bengali:</b> বিনামূল্যে কিছুই পাওয়া যায় না<br><b>English:</b> Nothing is given to you without some expectation of something in return<br><b>Example:</b> He's offering to help, but there's no such thing as a free lunch.	
Thin On The Ground	<b>Bengali:</b> বিরল, কদাচিৎ দেখা যায়<br><b>English:</b> Rare, seldom encountered<br><b>Example:</b> Good employees are thin on the ground these days.	
Third Time's a Charm	<b>Bengali:</b> তৃতীয়বারে সফল হওয়ার সম্ভাবনা<br><b>English:</b> Even if you fail at something twice, you may well succeed the third time<br><b>Example:</b> I failed the driving test twice, but third time's a charm!	
Three Sheets to the Wind	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব মাতাল<br><b>English:</b> Very drunk<br><b>Example:</b> By the end of the party, he was three sheets to the wind.	
Throw Caution to the Wind	<b>Bengali:</b> সাহসিকতার সাথে কাজ করা, বিবেচনা ছাড়া<br><b>English:</b> To act in a daring way, without forethought<br><b>Example:</b> He threw caution to the wind and quit his job to travel.	
Rob the Cradle	<b>Bengali:</b> বয়সে অনেক ছোট কারো সাথে সম্পর্ক<br><b>English:</b> To be sexually or romantically involved with someone who is very young<br><b>Example:</b> At 45, dating a 22-year-old is really robbing the cradle.	
Rock Bottom	<b>Bengali:</b> একেবারে নিচু অবস্থা<br><b>English:</b> An absolute low point<br><b>Example:</b> After losing his job and home, he hit rock bottom.	
Rubber-Stamp	<b>Bengali:</b> বিবেচনা ছাড়াই অনুমোদন দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Approve something without consideration, as a formality<br><b>Example:</b> The board just rubber-stamped the CEO's proposal.	
Rule of Thumb	<b>Bengali:</b> সাধারণ নিয়ম বা নির্দেশনা<br><b>English:</b> A general principle or guideline, not a specific formula<br><b>Example:</b> The rule of thumb is to save 10% of your income.	
Run a Tight Ship	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠোরভাবে সংস্থা পরিচালনা করা<br><b>English:</b> Manage an organization in a strict, well-regulated way<br><b>Example:</b> The new principal runs a tight ship - no nonsense allowed.	
Run off at the Mouth	<b>Bengali:</b> অপ্রয়োজনীয় কথা বলা<br><b>English:</b> Talk a lot about unimportant things, talk incoherently<br><b>Example:</b> He tends to run off at the mouth when he's nervous.	
Run on Fumes	<b>Bengali:</b> শক্তি বা সম্পদ প্রায় শেষ<br><b>English:</b> To be in a situation where one's energy or resources is almost exhausted<br><b>Example:</b> After working 16 hours, I'm running on fumes.	
Run Out of Steam	<b>Bengali:</b> গতি হারানো, ক্লান্ত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Lose momentum, become tired<br><b>Example:</b> The protest movement ran out of steam after a few weeks.	
Scorched Earth	<b>Bengali:</b> নির্দয়, অত্যন্ত ধ্বংসাত্মক<br><b>English:</b> Ruthless, extremely destructive<br><b>Example:</b> The company used scorched earth tactics against its competitors.	
Second Stringer	<b>Bengali:</b> বিকল্প খেলোয়াড়<br><b>English:</b> A substitute player in a sport; a substitute for a job who is not the most talented person<br><b>Example:</b> After the injury, the second stringer had to play.	
Second Wind	<b>Bengali:</b> নতুন শক্তি<br><b>English:</b> Renewed energy<br><b>Example:</b> After resting briefly, the runner got her second wind.	
See Eye to Eye	<b>Bengali:</b> একমত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To concur, agree<br><b>Example:</b> We don't always see eye to eye, but we respect each other.	
Set the Thames on Fire	<b>Bengali:</b> অসাধারণ কিছু করা (সাধারণত নেতিবাচক)<br><b>English:</b> Do something amazing. Usually used in the negative<br><b>Example:</b> He's competent, but he'll never set the Thames on fire.	
Shake the Dust off Your Shoes	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্পর্ক বা পরিস্থিতির সাথে পুরোপুরি ছেদ<br><b>English:</b> Make a clean break with a relationship or situation<br><b>Example:</b> After the toxic job, I shook the dust off my shoes and moved on.	
Sharp as A Tack	<b>Bengali:</b> মানসিকভাবে তীক্ষ্ণ<br><b>English:</b> Mentally agile<br><b>Example:</b> Despite being 90, my grandmother is still sharp as a tack.	
Shift Gears	<b>Bengali:</b> বিষয় পরিবর্তন করা<br><b>English:</b> Change the subject, or change what one is doing<br><b>Example:</b> Let's shift gears and talk about something more pleasant.	
Shipshape And Bristol Fashion	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিচ্ছন্ন ও গোছানো<br><b>English:</b> Tidy, clean<br><b>Example:</b> The admiral wants everything shipshape and Bristol fashion.	
Shoot Oneself In The Foot	<b>Bengali:</b> নিজের ক্ষতি করা<br><b>English:</b> Do something that damages oneself or one's own cause<br><b>Example:</b> By lying to the boss, he shot himself in the foot.	
Show One's True Colors	<b>Bengali:</b> আসল চরিত্র প্রকাশ করা<br><b>English:</b> Reveal one's true nature<br><b>Example:</b> When the pressure mounted, he showed his true colors.	
Sick as a Parrot	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব হতাশ<br><b>English:</b> Very disappointed<br><b>Example:</b> When his team lost, he was sick as a parrot.	
Sight for Sore Eyes	<b>Bengali:</b> আনন্দদায়ক দৃশ্য<br><b>English:</b> A sight that makes you happy<br><b>Example:</b> After being away for months, home was a sight for sore eyes.	
Sink or Swim	<b>Bengali:</b> ব্যর্থ বা সফল হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Fail or succeed<br><b>Example:</b> At this company, it's sink or swim from day one.	
Sitting Duck	<b>Bengali:</b> সহজ লক্ষ্য<br><b>English:</b> Something or someone easily attacked or criticized<br><b>Example:</b> Without bodyguards, the celebrity was a sitting duck.	
Sitting Pretty	<b>Bengali:</b> সুবিধাজনক অবস্থানে<br><b>English:</b> In a favorable situation<br><b>Example:</b> With his trust fund, he's sitting pretty for life.	
Six of One, a Half Dozen of the Other	<b>Bengali:</b> দুটি পছন্দে কোনো বড় পার্থক্য নেই<br><b>English:</b> The two choices have no significant differences<br><b>Example:</b> Taking the bus or the train? It's six of one, half dozen of the other.	
Sleep Like a Baby	<b>Bengali:</b> গভীর ঘুম<br><b>English:</b> To experience a very deep and restful sleep; to sleep soundly<br><b>Example:</b> After the long hike, I slept like a baby.	
Sleep with the Fishes	<b>Bengali:</b> মৃত, প্রায়ই হত্যার মাধ্যমে<br><b>English:</b> Dead, often by murder<br><b>Example:</b> Cross the mafia and you'll sleep with the fishes.	
Slippery Slope	<b>Bengali:</b> বিপজ্জনক ধারাবাহিক পরিণতি<br><b>English:</b> A series of undesirable effects that, one warns, could result from a certain action<br><b>Example:</b> Allowing this exception could be a slippery slope.	
Small Beer	<b>Bengali:</b> গুরুত্বহীন<br><b>English:</b> Unimportant, insignificant<br><b>Example:</b> Losing five dollars is small beer compared to your salary.	
Small Potatoes	<b>Bengali:</b> তুচ্ছ বিষয়<br><b>English:</b> Unimportant, insignificant<br><b>Example:</b> A thousand dollars sounds like small potatoes to a millionaire.	
Smell a Rat	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতারণার সন্দেহ করা<br><b>English:</b> Suspect deception<br><b>Example:</b> When the deal seemed too good to be true, I smelled a rat.	
Snake Oil	<b>Bengali:</b> নকল ওষুধ, অকার্যকর সমাধান<br><b>English:</b> A useless medicine; a quack remedy; a product or measure promoted as a solution that really does nothing to help<br><b>Example:</b> That weight loss pill is pure snake oil.	
Sold On (Something)	<b>Bengali:</b> কোনো বিষয়ে নিশ্চিত<br><b>English:</b> Convinced of something<br><b>Example:</b> After the demo, I'm sold on this new software.	
Son of a Gun	<b>Bengali:</b> দুষ্টু ব্যক্তি; বিস্ময়সূচক শব্দ<br><b>English:</b> A rogue. An exclamation of surprise<br><b>Example:</b> Well, I'll be a son of a gun - look who's here!	
Speak with A Plum in One's Mouth	<b>Bengali:</b> উঁচু শ্রেণীর মতো কথা বলা<br><b>English:</b> To speak in a manner that is indicative of a high social class<br><b>Example:</b> She speaks with a plum in her mouth, trying to sound aristocratic.	
Spoiling for a Fight	<b>Bengali:</b> লড়াইয়ের জন্য উদ্গ্রীব<br><b>English:</b> Combative, wanting conflict, eager to argue or fight<br><b>Example:</b> He's been spoiling for a fight all evening.	
Stab Someone in the Back	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো সাথে বিশ্বাসঘাতকতা করা<br><b>English:</b> To betray (somebody)<br><b>Example:</b> I trusted him, but he stabbed me in the back.	
Stand One's Ground	<b>Bengali:</b> নিজের অবস্থানে অটল থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Refuse to back down; insist on one's position<br><b>Example:</b> Despite the pressure, she stood her ground.	
"Stem the Tide	""<b>Bengali:</b> অনিষ্টকর কিছুর বৃদ্ধি রোধ করা<br><b>English:</b> To stop or control the growth of something"," usually something unpleasant<br><b>Example:</b> The government tried to stem the tide of unemployment.""""Pushing Up Daisies""	"
Put a Thumb on the Scale	<b>Bengali:</b> অন্যায়ভাবে আলোচনায় প্রভাব বিস্তার করার চেষ্টা, প্রতারণা করা<br><b>English:</b> Try to influence a discussion in an unfair way, cheat<br><b>Example:</b> The judge put a thumb on the scale by favoring one side.	
Put Down Roots	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি জায়গায় নিজেকে প্রতিষ্ঠিত করা; বসতি স্থাপন করা<br><b>English:</b> Establish oneself in a place; settle<br><b>Example:</b> After years of traveling, they decided to put down roots in Portland.	
Put in One's Two Cents	<b>Bengali:</b> আপনার মতামত বলা<br><b>English:</b> Say your opinion<br><b>Example:</b> If I may put in my two cents, I think we should postpone the meeting.	
Put Out Feelers	<b>Bengali:</b> বিচক্ষণ, অনানুষ্ঠানিক পরামর্শ দেওয়া, খোঁজখবর নেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Make discreet, informal suggestions, ask around<br><b>Example:</b> I'm putting out feelers about job opportunities in other companies.	
Put That in Your Pipe and Smoke It	<b>Bengali:</b> আমি যা বলছি তা গ্রহণ করুন এবং বিবেচনা করুন, যদিও আপনার পছন্দ না হয়!<br><b>English:</b> Accept and consider what I'm saying, even if you don't like it!<br><b>Example:</b> I got the promotion you wanted - put that in your pipe and smoke it!	
Put the Best Face On (Something)	<b>Bengali:</b> খারাপ পরিস্থিতির ইতিবাচক দিকগুলির উপর জোর দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Emphasize the positive aspects of a bad situation<br><b>Example:</b> Despite the layoffs, the CEO tried to put the best face on the company's restructuring.	
Put the Genie Back in the Bottle	<b>Bengali:</b> ইতিমধ্যে প্রকাশিত বা সম্পন্ন হওয়া কিছু দমন করার চেষ্টা করা<br><b>English:</b> Try to suppress something that has already been revealed or done<br><b>Example:</b> Once the scandal broke, there was no putting the genie back in the bottle.	
Put Up with (Something)	<b>Bengali:</b> সহ্য করা, মেনে নেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Tolerate, accept<br><b>Example:</b> I won't put up with this rude behavior anymore.	
Put Your Foot Down	<b>Bengali:</b> নেতিবাচক আচরণ বন্ধ করতে আপনার কর্তৃত্ব ব্যবহার করা<br><b>English:</b> Use your authority to stop negative behavior<br><b>Example:</b> When the kids got too rowdy, mom put her foot down.	
Quick as a Flash	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব দ্রুত<br><b>English:</b> Very fast<br><b>Example:</b> Quick as a flash, the cat caught the mouse.	
Quick-and-Dirty	<b>Bengali:</b> আনুমানিক, তাড়াহুড়ো করে করা<br><b>English:</b> Approximate, hastily done<br><b>Example:</b> I need a quick-and-dirty estimate of the costs.	
Quote Unquote	<b>Bengali:</b> ব্যঙ্গাত্মকভাবে বলা<br><b>English:</b> Ironically speaking; suggesting that if a phrase were written out, it would be in quotation marks to convey sarcasm<br><b>Example:</b> He's a quote unquote expert, but he doesn't know much.	
Race Against Time	<b>Bengali:</b> সময়ের বিরুদ্ধে দৌড়, নির্দিষ্ট সময়ে শেষ করার জন্য তাড়াহুড়ো করা<br><b>English:</b> To rush to meet a deadline, to be forced to do something very quickly<br><b>Example:</b> It's a race against time to finish the project before the deadline.	
Rain on Someone's Parade	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো পরিকল্পনা নষ্ট করা<br><b>English:</b> Spoil someone's plans<br><b>Example:</b> I don't want to rain on your parade, but that idea won't work.	
Rear Its Ugly Head	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যা বা অপ্রীতিকর কিছু প্রকাশ পাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Appear, be revealed (said of a problem or something unpleasant)<br><b>Example:</b> The corruption scandal reared its ugly head again.	
Red Flag	<b>Bengali:</b> সতর্কবাণী, বিপদের লক্ষণ<br><b>English:</b> A warning; a sign of trouble ahead<br><b>Example:</b> His reluctance to discuss finances was a red flag.	
Riding High	<b>Bengali:</b> সাফল্যের শীর্ষে থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Enjoying success<br><b>Example:</b> After the big contract, the company is riding high.	
Right Under (One's) Nose	<b>Bengali:</b> সামনেই থাকা কিন্তু লক্ষ্য না করা<br><b>English:</b> In an obvious location, yet overlooked<br><b>Example:</b> The keys were right under my nose the whole time.	
Ring a Bell	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিচিত লাগা<br><b>English:</b> Sound familiar<br><b>Example:</b> That name rings a bell, but I can't place where I've heard it.	
No Names, No Pack Drill	<b>Bengali:</b> কাউকে চিহ্নিত করা না গেলে কেউ শাস্তি পাবে না<br><b>English:</b> If no one can be identified, no one will be punished<br><b>Example:</b> I heard someone was stealing from the petty cash, but no names, no pack drill.	
No Room to Swing A Cat	<b>Bengali:</b> খুবই ছোট, যথেষ্ট বড় নয়<br><b>English:</b> Very small, not big enough<br><b>Example:</b> The apartment is tiny - no room to swing a cat.	
No Shit, Sherlock	<b>Bengali:</b> এটা খুবই স্পষ্ট!<br><b>English:</b> That's very obvious!<br><b>Example:</b> You figured out that water is wet? No shit, Sherlock!	
Not Have A Cat In Hell's Chance	<b>Bengali:</b> সফল হওয়া, ঘটা, বা কিছু অর্জনের কোন সম্ভাবনা নেই<br><b>English:</b> Have no possibility of succeeding, coming to pass, or achieving something<br><b>Example:</b> He doesn't have a cat in hell's chance of winning that race.	
Not Have a Prayer	<b>Bengali:</b> সফলতার কোন সুযোগ নেই<br><b>English:</b> Have no chance of success<br><b>Example:</b> Against that experienced team, we don't have a prayer.	
Not Know Jack	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছুই জানা নেই<br><b>English:</b> Not know anything<br><b>Example:</b> When it comes to car engines, I don't know jack.	
Not Lift a Finger	<b>Bengali:</b> সাহায্য করতে কিছুই না করা<br><b>English:</b> Do nothing to help<br><b>Example:</b> While we cleaned the house, he didn't lift a finger to help.	
Not Playing with A Full Deck	<b>Bengali:</b> বোকা, মানসিকভাবে ঘাটতিযুক্ত বা প্রতিবন্ধী<br><b>English:</b> Stupid, mentally deficient or impaired<br><b>Example:</b> Anyone who believes that conspiracy theory isn't playing with a full deck.	
Nothing to Write Home About	<b>Bengali:</b> অসাধারণ নয়, সাধারণ<br><b>English:</b> Unspectacular, ordinary<br><b>Example:</b> The movie was okay, but nothing to write home about.	
Pack Heat	<b>Bengali:</b> বন্দুক বহন করা<br><b>English:</b> Carry a gun<br><b>Example:</b> In that dangerous neighborhood, many people pack heat for protection.	
Paddle One's Own Canoe	<b>Bengali:</b> স্বাধীনভাবে কাজ করতে সক্ষম হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To be able to act independently<br><b>Example:</b> Since graduating, she's learned to paddle her own canoe.	
Page-Turner	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি উত্তেজনাপূর্ণ বই যা পড়তে সহজ, একটি বই যা রাখা কঠিন<br><b>English:</b> A page-turner is an exciting book that's easy to read, a book that's difficult to put down<br><b>Example:</b> That mystery novel was a real page-turner - I finished it in one sitting.	
Paint the Town Red	<b>Bengali:</b> পানীয় এবং পার্টির জন্য বাইরে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Go out drinking and partying<br><b>Example:</b> After finals, the students painted the town red.	
Pass With Flying Colors	<b>Bengali:</b> উজ্জ্বলভাবে সফল হওয়া, যেমন পরীক্ষা বা অন্য পরীক্ষায়<br><b>English:</b> To succeed brilliantly, as on an exam or other test<br><b>Example:</b> She passed her driving test with flying colors.	
Peaches and Cream	<b>Bengali:</b> এমন পরিস্থিতি, প্রক্রিয়া, ইত্যাদি যার কোনো সমস্যা বা অসুবিধা নেই<br><b>English:</b> A situation, process, etc., that has no trouble or problems<br><b>Example:</b> Marriage isn't always peaches and cream - it takes work.	
Pecking Order	<b>Bengali:</b> স্তরবিন্যাস, গুরুত্বের ক্রম<br><b>English:</b> Hierarchy, rank of importance<br><b>Example:</b> In the corporate pecking order, she ranks quite high.	
Penny-Pinching	<b>Bengali:</b> মিতব্যয়ী, যখনই সম্ভব খরচ এড়ানো<br><b>English:</b> Frugal, avoiding expenses whenever possible<br><b>Example:</b> His penny-pinching ways helped him save for retirement.	
Pick Up the Slack	<b>Bengali:</b> অন্য কেউ যা করছে না তা করা; অন্য কারো দায়িত্ব গ্রহণ করা<br><b>English:</b> Do something that someone else is not doing; assume someone else's responsibilities<br><b>Example:</b> When John quit, the rest of us had to pick up the slack.	
Pick Up the Tab	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি গ্রুপের কাছে উপস্থাপিত বিল পরিশোধ করা, বিশেষ করে রেস্তোরাঁ বা বারে<br><b>English:</b> To pay a bill presented to a group, especially in a restaurant or bar<br><b>Example:</b> Don't worry about dinner - the company will pick up the tab.	
Pin Someone Down	<b>Bengali:</b> সিদ্ধান্ত বা স্পষ্ট উত্তরের দাবি<br><b>English:</b> Demand a decision or clear answer<br><b>Example:</b> I tried to pin him down on a delivery date, but he was evasive.	
Pinch Pennies	<b>Bengali:</b> অর্থের সাথে সতর্ক থাকা, মিতব্যয়ী হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To be careful with money, to be thrifty<br><b>Example:</b> Since losing his job, he's been pinching pennies to make ends meet.	
Pink Slip	<b>Bengali:</b> ছাঁটাইয়ের নোটিস; চাকরি হারানো, সাধারণত ছাঁটাইয়ের কারণে<br><b>English:</b> A layoff notice; loss of a job, typically because of layoffs<br><b>Example:</b> Many employees got pink slips when the company downsized.	
Pipe Dream	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি অবাস্তব আশা, একটি কল্পনা<br><b>English:</b> An unrealistic hope, a fantasy<br><b>Example:</b> Winning the lottery is just a pipe dream for most people.	
Pissing Contest	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি অর্থহীন তর্ক বা প্রতিযোগিতা, সাধারণত পুরুষদের মধ্যে<br><b>English:</b> A meaningless argument or competition, typically between males<br><b>Example:</b> Their argument about whose car is faster is just a pissing contest.	
Play Ball	<b>Bengali:</b> সহযোগিতা করা, অংশগ্রহণে সম্মত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Cooperate, agree to participate<br><b>Example:</b> If you want this deal to work, you need to play ball.	
Play Hardball	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠোর আলোচনার অবস্থান গ্রহণ করা; আক্রমণাত্মকভাবে কাজ করা<br><b>English:</b> Adopt a tough negotiating position; act aggressively<br><b>Example:</b> When the union wouldn't budge, management decided to play hardball.	
Play It by Ear	<b>Bengali:</b> নির্দিষ্ট পরিকল্পনার পরিবর্তে পরিস্থিতি অনুযায়ী সাড়া দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To respond to circumstances instead of having a fixed plan<br><b>Example:</b> We don't have reservations, so we'll just play it by ear.	
Play the Ponies	<b>Bengali:</b> ঘোড়দৌড়ে বাজি ধরা<br><b>English:</b> Bet on horse racing<br><b>Example:</b> Every weekend, he goes to the track to play the ponies.	
Play Your Cards Right	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি পরিস্থিতিকে নিজের সর্বোচ্চ সুবিধার জন্য কাজে লাগানো<br><b>English:</b> Exploit a situation to your best advantage<br><b>Example:</b> If you play your cards right, you could get that promotion.	
Point of No Return	<b>Bengali:</b> এমন জায়গা যেখান থেকে শুরুর স্থানে ফিরে যাওয়া অসম্ভব<br><b>English:</b> A place from which it is impossible to go back to the starting point<br><b>Example:</b> Once we sign the contract, we'll reach the point of no return.	
Poison Pill	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি ব্যবস্থা বা সত্তাকে কম আকর্ষণীয় করার জন্য যোগ করা বিধান বা বৈশিষ্ট্য, একটি অবাঞ্ছিত সংযোজন<br><b>English:</b> A provision or feature added to a measure or an entity to make it less attractive, an undesirable add-on<br><b>Example:</b> The company added a poison pill to prevent the hostile takeover.	
Pop the Question	<b>Bengali:</b> বিবাহের প্রস্তাব দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Propose marriage<br><b>Example:</b> After dating for three years, he finally popped the question.	
Powder Keg	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি বিস্ফোরক পরিস্থিতি, এমন পরিস্থিতি যেখানে মানুষ রাগান্বিত এবং হিংসাত্মক হতে প্রস্তুত<br><b>English:</b> An explosive situation, a situation in which people are angry and ready to be violent<br><b>Example:</b> The protest was a powder keg waiting to explode.	
Powder One's Nose	<b>Bengali:</b> বাথরুম ব্যবহার করা। এটি মহিলারা ব্যবহার করেন<br><b>English:</b> To use the restroom (lavatory). This is used by women<br><b>Example:</b> Excuse me, I need to powder my nose before the meeting.	
Price Yourself Out of the Market	<b>Bengali:</b> এত বেশি দামে পণ্য বা সেবা বিক্রি করার চেষ্টা করা যে কেউ কিনে না<br><b>English:</b> Try to sell goods or services at such a high price that nobody buys them<br><b>Example:</b> If you charge too much for consulting, you'll price yourself out of the market.	
Puddle Jumper	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি ছোট বিমান, ছোট ভ্রমণে ব্যবহৃত<br><b>English:</b> A small airplane, used on short trips<br><b>Example:</b> We took a puddle jumper from the main airport to the island.	
Pull Out All the Stops	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু সম্পন্ন করার জন্য সবকিছু সম্ভব করা<br><b>English:</b> Do everything possible to accomplish something<br><b>Example:</b> For their wedding, they pulled out all the stops.	
Puppies And Rainbows	<b>Bengali:</b> নিখুঁত, আদর্শ (সাধারণত সামান্য ব্যঙ্গাত্মকভাবে ব্যবহৃত, কম আদর্শ পরিস্থিতির বিপরীতে)<br><b>English:</b> Perfect, ideal (usually used slightly sarcastically, in contrast with a less ideal situation)<br><b>Example:</b> Life isn't all puppies and rainbows - there are real problems to face.	
Puppy Love	<b>Bengali:</b> কিশোর প্রেম বা মোহ, বিশেষ করে যা দীর্ঘস্থায়ী হওয়ার প্রত্যাশা নেই<br><b>English:</b> Adolescent love or infatuation, especially one that is not expected to last<br><b>Example:</b> Their teenage romance was just puppy love.	
Pure as the Driven Snow	<b>Bengali:</b> নিষ্পাপ এবং পবিত্র হওয়া (প্রায়ই ব্যঙ্গাত্মকভাবে ব্যবহৃত)<br><b>English:</b> To be innocent and chaste (frequently used ironically)<br><b>Example:</b> She acts like she's pure as the driven snow, but we know better.	
Push the Envelope	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু করার সাধারণ উপায়ের বাইরে যাওয়া, উদ্ভাবনী হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Go beyond common ways of doing something, be innovative<br><b>Example:</b> The artist likes to push the envelope with controversial subjects.	
Pushing Up Daisies	<b>Bengali:</b> মৃত এবং সমাধিস্থ<br><b>English:</b> Dead and buried<br><b>Example:</b> By the time that investment pays off, I'll be pushing up daisies.Front	
Mad As A Box Of (Soapy) Frogs	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত মানসিকভাবে অস্থির; মানসিক রোগী; বাস্তবতা থেকে বিচ্ছিন্ন<br><b>English:</b> Extremely mentally unstable; psychotic; detached from reality<br><b>Example:</b> After the accident, he went mad as a box of frogs.	
Mad as A Hatter	<b>Bengali:</b> মানসিকভাবে অসুস্থ, মানসিক রোগী<br><b>English:</b> Mentally ill, psychotic<br><b>Example:</b> The old hermit is mad as a hatter, talking to imaginary friends.	
Main Squeeze	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতিশ্রুতিবদ্ধ রোমান্টিক সঙ্গী<br><b>English:</b> Committed romantic partner<br><b>Example:</b> I'd like you to meet my main squeeze, Sarah.	
Make a Break for It	<b>Bengali:</b> পালানোর চেষ্টা করা, দৌড়ে পালানো<br><b>English:</b> Try to escape, run off<br><b>Example:</b> When the guard wasn't looking, the prisoner made a break for it.	
Make Ends Meet	<b>Bengali:</b> মৌলিক খরচ মেটানোর জন্য যথেষ্ট অর্থ থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Have enough money to cover basic expenses<br><b>Example:</b> With rising prices, it's getting harder to make ends meet.	
Make Hay (While the Sun Shines)	<b>Bengali:</b> সঠিক সময়ে সুযোগের সদ্ব্যবহার করা<br><b>English:</b> To take advantage of an opportunity at the right time<br><b>Example:</b> Business is good right now, so let's make hay while the sun shines.	
Make Love	<b>Bengali:</b> যৌন মিলন করা<br><b>English:</b> To have sexual intercourse<br><b>Example:</b> The romantic scene implied they made love, but didn't show it explicitly.	
Make Nice	<b>Bengali:</b> দ্বন্দ্ব সত্ত্বেও সৌহার্দ্যপূর্ণ আচরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> Act cordial despite conflict<br><b>Example:</b> Even though they hate each other, they make nice at family gatherings.	
Make Waves	<b>Bengali:</b> বিতর্ক সৃষ্টি করা, শান্ত গ্রুপের গতিশীলতা বিঘ্নিত করা<br><b>English:</b> Cause controversy, disturb a calm group dynamic<br><b>Example:</b> Don't make waves on your first day at the new job.	
Man Cave	<b>Bengali:</b> বাড়ির একটি অংশ, প্রায়ই বেসমেন্ট, যা ঘরের পুরুষের জন্য রাখা হয়<br><b>English:</b> A part of the house, often the basement, that is left to the man of the household<br><b>Example:</b> He retreated to his man cave to watch the game.	
March to the Beat of Your Own Drum	<b>Bengali:</b> যখন কেউ নিজের মতো করে কাজ করে, অন্য কাউকে বা কিছুকে বিবেচনায় না এনে<br><b>English:</b> When someone does things the way they want to, without taking anybody else or anything else into consideration<br><b>Example:</b> She's always marched to the beat of her own drum, never following trends.	
Match Made in Heaven	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি সম্পর্ক যেখানে দুজন একসাথে দুর্দান্ত, কারণ তারা একে অপরের খুব ভাল পরিপূরক<br><b>English:</b> A relationship in which the two people are great together, because they complement each other so well<br><b>Example:</b> John and Mary are a match made in heaven - they're perfect for each other.	
May-December Marriage	<b>Bengali:</b> একজন তরুণ ও একজন বয়স্ক সঙ্গীর মধ্যে বিবাহ, সাধারণত একজন তরুণী ও একজন বৃদ্ধ পুরুষ<br><b>English:</b> A marriage between a younger and an older partner, typically a young woman and an old man<br><b>Example:</b> Their May-December marriage raised eyebrows, but they're truly happy.	
Me Time	<b>Bengali:</b> নিজের উপভোগের জন্য গৃহীত কার্যকলাপ, অন্যদের প্রতি দায়বদ্ধতা থেকে মুক্ত<br><b>English:</b> Activities undertaken for one's own enjoyment, free from responsibilities to others<br><b>Example:</b> After a stressful week, I need some me time to relax.	
Mend Fences	<b>Bengali:</b> বিরোধের পর সম্পর্ক উন্নত করা<br><b>English:</b> Improve relations after a dispute<br><b>Example:</b> After their argument, they worked hard to mend fences.	
Mind One's P's and Q's	<b>Bengali:</b> বিস্তারিত বিষয়ে মনোযোগী হওয়া; নিজের সর্বোত্তম আচরণে থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Be attentive to details; be on one's best behavior<br><b>Example:</b> At the formal dinner, make sure to mind your P's and Q's.	
Month of Sundays	<b>Bengali:</b> দীর্ঘ সময়, অনেক মাস<br><b>English:</b> A long time, many months<br><b>Example:</b> It'll take a month of Sundays to clean up this mess.	
Move Up in the World	<b>Bengali:</b> আরো সফল হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Become more successful<br><b>Example:</b> Since getting her MBA, she's really moved up in the world.	
Movers and Shakers	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রভাবশালী ব্যক্তিরা, বিশেষ করে একটি নির্দিষ্ট ক্ষেত্রে<br><b>English:</b> Influential people, especially in a particular field<br><b>Example:</b> All the movers and shakers in Hollywood attended the premiere.	
Much Of A Muchness	<b>Bengali:</b> মূলত সমান, উল্লেখযোগ্যভাবে ভিন্ন নয় (একটি পছন্দের ক্ষেত্রে বলা হয়)<br><b>English:</b> Essentially equal, not significantly different (said of a choice)<br><b>Example:</b> Both restaurants are much of a muchness - either one would be fine.	
Mum's the Word	<b>Bengali:</b> এটি একটি গোপনীয়তা; এই বিষয়ে কথা বলবেন না<br><b>English:</b> This is a secret; don't talk about this<br><b>Example:</b> I'm planning a surprise party, so mum's the word.	
Music to My Ears	<b>Bengali:</b> শুনতে ভালো; স্বাগত সংবাদ<br><b>English:</b> Good to hear; welcome news<br><b>Example:</b> When she said I got the job, it was music to my ears.	
Mutton Dressed Up as Lamb	<b>Bengali:</b> একজন মহিলা যিনি কম বয়সীদের উপযুক্ত পোশাক পরেন<br><b>English:</b> A woman who dresses in a style appropriate to someone of a younger age<br><b>Example:</b> At 60, wearing a mini skirt makes her look like mutton dressed up as lamb.	
My Dogs Are Barking	<b>Bengali:</b> আমার পা ব্যথা করছে<br><b>English:</b> My feet hurt<br><b>Example:</b> After walking all day, my dogs are barking.	
My Old Man, My Old Lady	<b>Bengali:</b> আমার স্ত্রী/স্বামী<br><b>English:</b> My spouse<br><b>Example:</b> I need to check with my old lady before making plans.	
My Way or the Highway	<b>Bengali:</b> আমি যেভাবে চাই সেভাবে না করলে তুমি চলে যেতে পারো বা অংশগ্রহণ করতে হবে না<br><b>English:</b> If you do not do things the way I want or require, then you can just leave or not participate<br><b>Example:</b> The dictatorial boss said it's my way or the highway.	
Neck and Neck	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতিযোগিতায় খুবই কাছাকাছি, দুটি সত্তার কেউই স্পষ্টভাবে এগিয়ে নেই<br><b>English:</b> Very close in a competition, with neither of two entities clearly in the lead<br><b>Example:</b> The two candidates are running neck and neck in the polls.	
Neck of the Woods	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি অঞ্চল, বিশেষ করে নিজের বাড়ির অঞ্চল<br><b>English:</b> A region, especially one's home region<br><b>Example:</b> What brings you to this neck of the woods?	
Never Look a Gift Horse in the Mouth	<b>Bengali:</b> উপহার ঘনিষ্ঠভাবে পরীক্ষা করা অভদ্রতা; উপহার ভদ্রভাবে গ্রহণ করুন<br><b>English:</b> It's rude to examine a gift closely; accept gifts politely<br><b>Example:</b> The free car has some problems, but never look a gift horse in the mouth.	
New Wrinkle	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি পরিস্থিতির নতুন দিক, একটি নতুন উন্নয়ন<br><b>English:</b> A novel aspect to a situation, a new development<br><b>Example:</b> The new evidence adds a new wrinkle to the case.	
Nickel and Dime	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত ছোট অঙ্কের উপর দর কষাকষি করা; নেতিবাচক উপায়ে আরো ভাল আর্থিক চুক্তি পাওয়ার চেষ্টা করা<br><b>English:</b> To negotiate over very small sums; to try to get a better financial deal, in a negative way<br><b>Example:</b> Don't nickel and dime me over a few dollars.	
Nine Times Out of Ten	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রায় সবসময়<br><b>English:</b> Almost always<br><b>Example:</b> Nine times out of ten, he's right about the weather.	
Nine-to-Five Job	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি অফিসের নিয়মিত কাজ যা স্ট্যান্ডার্ড অফিস আওয়ার জড়িত<br><b>English:</b> A routine job in an office that involves standard office hours<br><b>Example:</b> After freelancing for years, she got a nine-to-five job for stability.	
No Holds Barred	<b>Bengali:</b> অবাধ, নিয়ম ছাড়া<br><b>English:</b> Unrestricted, without rules<br><b>Example:</b> The debate was no holds barred - they discussed everything.
